## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations and dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the features (x, v, t) match second-order oscillator models x'' = f(x, x', t). Common structures include restoring forces (linear and nonlinear in x), dissipation (terms in v), and external/parametric driving (explicit functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring acceleration)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven oscillator with phase: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (sinusoidal forcing with phase offset)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with damping)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear stiffness with drive)
- Pendulum equation (angle-as-position): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (nonlinear restoring torque with damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillation / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v - c2 * x (velocity-dependent energy injection/removal)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (turbulent-like drag)
- Dry (Coulomb) friction oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * (v / (Abs(v) + c3)) (regularized sign(v) friction)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / parametric resonance)
- Time-dependent damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * v (periodically modulated dissipation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear restoring force near equilibrium → dv_dt contains a term -c * x (small-amplitude approximation).
- Amplitude-dependent frequency/backbone curve → include odd stiffness nonlinearities like -c * x**3 (Duffing hardening/softening).
- Dissipation proportional to speed (laminar/viscous) → include -c * v; dissipation stronger at high speed → -c * v * Abs(v) or -c * v**3.
- Self-excited oscillations/limit cycles → negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, e.g., (c - x**2) * v (Van der Pol form).
- External periodic forcing → additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) term; resonance occurs when drive frequency matches natural frequency.
- Parametric resonance → multiplicative modulation of stiffness, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t)) * x, leading to instability tongues.
- Non-smooth frictional effects → dependence on sign(v); in smooth regression often approximated by v/(Abs(v)+c) or tanh(c*v).
- Conservative oscillator (no damping/forcing) → dv_dt depends primarily on x (and not explicitly on v or t), implying approximate energy conservation.

Expanding the GT:
`-3.42786200841899*x - 0.119969938498498*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) + 0.100299255716928*sin(t) - 0.888494670723871*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`
3. `sin(t)` (equivalently `cos(t + phase)`)
4. `sin(v)`

Key observation: **sin(v)** is a critical basis function. It cannot be represented by polynomials in v, v*Abs(v), v**3, v*Abs(v)**2, etc. The Taylor series of sin(v) = v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ..., but a finite polynomial can never exactly equal sin(v).

Similarly, `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` is a specific basis function, and `x*log(c*Abs(v)+1)` is NOT equivalent to it for any constant choice.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `sin(v)` (or equivalent):

**None of the candidates contain sin(v) or cos(v) as a function of v alone.**

All candidates use combinations of:
- `v` (linear), `v**3`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v*Abs(v)**2`, `v*Abs(v)**4`, `v/(c+Abs(v))`, etc.
- `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` or `x*log(c*Abs(v)+1)`
- `cos(c*t + c)` or `sin(c*t + c)` (functions of t, not v)
- Various other terms

Since `sin(v)` is linearly independent from all polynomial/rational/power-law functions of v, **no finite combination of these basis functions can exactly reproduce sin(v)**.

Let me verify there's no candidate with a `sin(v)` or `cos(v)` term... Going through all 50 candidates carefully:

- Trigonometric functions appear only as `cos(c*t+c)`, `sin(c*t+c)`, `cos(c*t)`, `sin(c*t)` — all functions of `t`, never of `v`.
- No candidate has `sin(v)` or `cos(v)`.

Therefore, **none of the candidates can match the GT**, because the GT requires a `sin(v)` term which is linearly independent from all the v-dependent basis functions present in any candidate.
